           </tr>

           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>et</code> Estonian</td> 
            <td><code>fi</code> Finnish</td> 
            <td><code>ka</code> Georgian</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>he</code> Hebrew</td> 
            <td><code>hu</code> Hungarian</td> 
            <td><code>is</code> Icelandic</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>ja</code> Japanese</td> 
            <td><code>ko</code> Korean</td> 
            <td><code>lt</code> Lithuanian</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>lv</code> Latvian</td> 
            <td><code>mn</code> Mongolian</td> 
            <td><code>nb</code> Norwegian Bokmål</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>pl</code> Polish</td> 
            <td><code>pt</code> Portuguese</td> 
            <td><code>ro</code> Romanian</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>ru</code> Russian</td> 
            <td><code>sk</code> Slovak</td> 
            <td><code>sl</code> Slovenian</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>sr</code> Serbian</td> 
            <td><code>sv</code> Swedish</td> 
            <td><code>tl</code> Tagalog</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>th</code> Thai</td> 
            <td><code>uk</code> Ukrainian</td> 
            <td><code>zh_Hans</code> Simplified Chinese</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>zh_Hant</code> Traditional Chinese</td>

           </tr>

         <p><strong>Limited coverage:</strong> <em>these languages are sometimes present but coverage tends to be inconsistent or geographically constrained</em></p> 
         <table>

           <tr> 
            <th>Language</th> 
            <th></th> 
            <th></th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>ar</code> Arabic</td> 
            <td><code>es</code> Spanish</td> 
            <td><code>fa</code> Persian</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>kk</code> Kazakh</td> 
            <td><code>ms</code> Malay</td> 
            <td><code>sq</code> Albanian</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>tr</code> Turkish</td> 
            <td><code>uz</code> Uzbek</td> 
            <td><code>vi</code> Vietnamese</td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table>

         <div class="endpoint dark fill-dark round "> 
          <div class="round-left pad0y pad1x fill-lighten0 code small endpoint-method">
           GET
          </div> 
          <div class="pad0 code small endpoint-url">
           /geocoding/v5/
           <span class="strong">{mode}</span>/
           <span class="strong">{query}</span>.json
          </div> 
         </div>

       <div data-title="Response object" class="keyline-top section contain clearfix " data-reactid="205">
        <div class="space-bottom8 col6 pad2x prose clip" data-reactid="206">
         <h3 id="response-object">Response object</h3> 
         <p>Because Mapbox's geocoding<a href="https://mapbox.com/help/define-geocoding/" title="Geocoding is the process of taking an address or name of a place and converting it into latitude and longitude values. The Mapbox Geocoding API allows you to performs two types of geocoding: forward geocoding and reverse geocoding." class="auto-glossary-link" rel="noreferrer" target="_blank">?</a> data is constantly updated and improved, the values of properties in the response object are not guaranteed and may change within the same version of the API. Properties may be added to but will not be removed from the response within the same version. Geocoding results are returned in <a href="https://github.com/mapbox/carmen/blob/master/carmen-geojson.md">Carmen GeoJSON</a> format.</p> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>Property</th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>type</code></td> 
            <td><code>"Feature Collection"</code> , a GeoJSON type from the <a href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc7946">GeoJSON specification</a> .</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>query</code></td> 
            <td>An array of space and punctuation-separated strings from the original query.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>features</code></td> 
            <td>An array of feature objects.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>attribution</code></td> 
            <td>A string attributing the results of the Mapbox Geocoding API to Mapbox and links to Mapbox's terms of service and data sources.</td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table> 
         <p><strong>Feature object</strong></p> 
         <p>Each feature object in the <code>"features"</code> array may have the properties described below. Forward geocodes return features ordered by <code>relevance</code>. Reverse geocodes return features in order of index hierarchy from most specific features to least specific features that overlap the queried coordinates.</p> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>Property</th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>id</code></td> 
            <td>A string feature id in the form <code>{type}.{id}</code> where <code>{type}</code> is the lowest hierarchy feature in the <code>place_type</code> field. The <code>{id}</code> suffix of the feature id is unstable and may change within versions.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>type</code></td> 
            <td><code>"Feature"</code> , a GeoJSON type from the <a href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc7946">GeoJSON specification</a> .</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>place_type</code></td> 
            <td>An array of feature types describing the feature. Options are <code>country</code> , <code>region</code> , <code>postcode</code> , <code>district</code> , <code>place</code> , <code>locality</code> , <code>neighborhood</code> , <code>address</code> , <code>poi</code> , and <code>poi.landmark</code> . Most features have only one type, but if the feature has multiple types, (for example, Vatican City is a <code>country</code> , <code>region</code> , and <code>place</code> ), all applicable types will be listed in the array.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>relevance</code></td> 
            <td>A numerical score from 0 (least relevant) to 0.99 (most relevant) measuring how well each returned feature matches the query. You can use the <code>relevance</code> property to remove results which don't fully match the query.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>address</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>A string of the house number for the returned <code>address</code> feature. Note that unlike the <code>address</code> property for <code>poi</code> features, this property is outside the <code>properties</code> object.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>properties</code></td> 
            <td>An object describing the feature. The property object is unstable and only <a href="https://github.com/mapbox/carmen/blob/master/carmen-geojson.md">Carmen GeoJSON</a> properties are guaranteed. Your implementation should check for the presence of these values in a response before it attempts to use them.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>properties.address</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>A string of the full street address for the returned <code>poi</code> feature. Note that unlike the <code>address</code> property for <code>address</code> features, this property is inside the <code>properties</code> object.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>properties.category</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>A string of comma-separated categories for the returned <code>poi</code> feature.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>properties.tel</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>A formatted string of the telephone number for the returned <code>poi</code> feature.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>properties.maki</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>The name of a suggested <a href="https://www.mapbox.com/maki-icons/">Maki</a> icon to visualize a <code>poi</code> feature based on its <code>category</code> .</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>properties.landmark</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>A boolean value indicating whether a <code>poi</code> feature is a landmark. Landmarks are particularly notable or long-lived features like schools, parks, museums and places of worship.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>properties.wikidata</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>The <a href="https://wikidata.org">Wikidata</a> identifier for the returned feature.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>properties.short_code</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISO_3166-1_alpha-2">ISO 3166-1</a> country and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISO_3166-2">ISO 3166-2</a> region code for the returned feature.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>text</code></td> 
            <td>A string representing the feature in the requested language, if specified.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>place_name</code></td> 
            <td>A string representing the feature in the requested language, if specified, and its full result hierarchy.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>matching_text</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>A string analogous to the <code>text</code> field that more closely matches the query than results in the specified language. For example, querying "Köln, Germany" with language set to English might return a feature with the <code>text</code> "Cologne" and the <code>matching_text</code> "Köln".</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>matching_place_name</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>A string analogous to the <code>place_name</code> field that more closely matches the query than results in the specified language. For example, querying "Köln, Germany" with language set to English might return a feature with the <code>place_name</code> "Cologne, Germany" and a <code>matching_place_name</code> of "Köln, North Rhine-Westphalia, Germany".</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>text_{language}</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>A string analogous to the <code>text</code> field that matches the query in the requested language. This field is only returned when requesting multiple languages and will be present for each requested language.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>place_name_{language}</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>A string analogous to the <code>place_name</code> field that matches the query in the requested language. This field is only returned when requesting multiple languages and will be present for each requested language.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>language</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>A string of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IETF_language_tag">IETF language tag</a> of the query's primary language.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>language_{language}</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>A string of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IETF_language_tag">IETF language tag</a> of the query's fallback language. This field is only returned when requesting multiple languages and will be present for each requested language.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>bbox</code></td> 
            <td>An array bounding box in the form [ minX,minY,maxX,maxY ] .</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>center</code></td> 
            <td>An array in the form [ longitude,latitude ] at the center of the specified <code>bbox</code> .</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>geometry</code></td> 
            <td>An object describing the spatial geometry of the returned feature.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>geometry.type</code></td> 
            <td><code>"Point"</code> , a GeoJSON type from the <a href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc7946">GeoJSON specification</a> .</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>geometry.coordinates</code></td> 
            <td>An array in the format [ longitude,latitude ] at the center of the specified <code>bbox</code> .</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>geometry.interpolated</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>A boolean value indicating if an <code>address</code> is interpolated along a road network. This field is only present when the feature is interpolated.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>context</code></td> 
            <td>An array representing the hierarchy of encompassing parent features. Each parent feature may include any of the above properties.</td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table> 
        </div>
        <div class="space-bottom4 col6 pad2 prose clip fill-light space-top5" data-reactid="207">

       <div data-title="Search for places" class="keyline-top section contain clearfix " data-reactid="208">
        <div class="space-bottom8 col6 pad2x prose clip" data-reactid="209">
         <h3 id="search-for-places">Search for places</h3> 
         <p>This is often called <strong>forward geocoding</strong>. Request feature data that best matches the input <code>{query}</code> text. The response includes one or more results ordered by relevance.</p> 
         <p>This API is used by the <a href="https://www.mapbox.com/mapbox.js/api/v2.3.0/l-mapbox-geocodercontrol/">Mapbox.js L.mapbox.geocoderControl</a> and the <a href="https://github.com/mapbox/mapbox-gl-geocoder">mapbox-gl-geocoder</a> user interfaces.</p> 
         <p><a href="https://www.mapbox.com/api-playground/#/forward-geocoding/">Try this in the API Playground</a>.</p> 
        </div>
        <div class="space-bottom4 col6 pad2 prose clip fill-light space-top5" data-reactid="210">
         <div class="endpoint dark fill-dark round "> 
          <div class="round-left pad0y pad1x fill-lighten0 code small endpoint-method">
           GET
          </div> 
          <div class="pad0 code small endpoint-url">
           /geocoding/v5/
           <span class="strong">{mode}</span>/
           <span class="strong">{query}</span>.json
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <h4 id="example-request-33">Example request</h4> 
         <pre class="hljs">$ curl <span class="hljs-string">"https://api.mapbox.com/geocoding/v5/mapbox.places/Los%20Angeles.json?access_token=<span class="token-widget"></span>"</span></pre> 
         <pre class="hljs">curl <span class="hljs-string">"https://api.mapbox.com/geocoding/v5/mapbox.places/2+lincoln+memorial+circle+nw.json?access_token=<span class="token-widget"></span>"</span>

<span class="hljs-comment"># use the country option to limit</span>
<span class="hljs-comment"># results to Canada and exclude the</span>
<span class="hljs-comment"># Lincoln Memorial in America</span>
curl <span class="hljs-string">"https://api.mapbox.com/geocoding/v5/mapbox.places/2+lincoln+memorial+circle+nw.json?country=ca&amp;access_token=<span class="token-widget"></span>"</span>

<span class="hljs-comment"># there are many towns named 'Chester', but adding the</span>
<span class="hljs-comment"># proximity parameter with local coordinates ensures that the town</span>
<span class="hljs-comment"># of Chester, New Jersey is in the search results</span>
curl <span class="hljs-string">"https://api.mapbox.com/geocoding/v5/mapbox.places/chester.json?proximity=-74.70850,40.78375&amp;access_token=<span class="token-widget"></span>"</span>

<span class="hljs-comment"># search only for countries named Georgia,</span>
<span class="hljs-comment"># so that we don't find the state in America</span>
curl <span class="hljs-string">"https://api.mapbox.com/geocoding/v5/mapbox.places/georgia.json?types=country&amp;access_token=<span class="token-widget"></span>"</span>

<span class="hljs-comment"># use the bounding box option to limit results for a</span>
<span class="hljs-comment"># search for "Starbucks" to those within Washington, D.C.</span>
curl <span class="hljs-string">"https://api.mapbox.com/geocoding/v5/mapbox.places/starbucks.json?bbox=-77.083056,38.908611,-76.997778,38.959167&amp;access_token=<span class="token-widget"></span>"</span>

<span class="hljs-comment"># use the limit option to limit the number of</span>
<span class="hljs-comment"># results to `2`. Even though there are many possible matches</span>
<span class="hljs-comment"># for `Washington`, this query will only return 2 results.</span>
curl <span class="hljs-string">"https://api.mapbox.com/geocoding/v5/mapbox.places/Washington.json?limit=2&amp;access_token=<span class="token-widget"></span>"</span></pre> 
        </div>
       </div>
       <div data-title="Retrieve places near a location" class="keyline-top section contain clearfix " data-reactid="211">
        <div class="space-bottom8 col6 pad2x prose clip" data-reactid="212">
         <h3 id="retrieve-places-near-a-location">Retrieve places near a location</h3> 
         <p>This is often called <strong>reverse geocoding</strong>. Request feature data located at the input <code>{longitude},{latitude}</code> coordinates. The response includes at most one result from each type, unless using the <code>limit</code> option.</p> 
         <p><a href="https://www.mapbox.com/api-playground/#/reverse-geocoding/">Try this in the API Playground</a>.</p> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>URL Parameter</th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>mode</code></td> 
            <td><code>mapbox.places</code> or <code>mapbox.places-permanent</code> for enterprise/batch geocoding (see Response format below).</td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>Query Parameter</th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>types</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>Filter results by one or more type. Options are <code>country</code> , <code>region</code> , <code>postcode</code> , <code>district</code> , <code>place</code> , <code>locality</code> , <code>neighborhood</code> , <code>address</code> , <code>poi</code> , and <code>poi.landmark</code> . Multiple options can be comma-separated. Note that <code>poi.landmark</code> returns a subset of the results returned by <code>poi</code> .</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>limit</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>Limit the maximum number of results. The default is <code>1</code> , and the maximum is <code>5</code> . If using this option a single <code>types</code> is required.</td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table> 
        </div>
        <div class="space-bottom4 col6 pad2 prose clip fill-light space-top5" data-reactid="213">
         <div class="endpoint dark fill-dark round "> 
          <div class="round-left pad0y pad1x fill-lighten0 code small endpoint-method">
           GET
          </div> 
          <div class="pad0 code small endpoint-url">
           /geocoding/v5/
           <span class="strong">{mode}</span>/
           <span class="strong">{longitude}</span>,
           <span class="strong">{latitude}</span>.json
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <h4 id="example-request-34">Example request</h4> 
         <pre class="hljs">curl <span class="hljs-string">"https://api.mapbox.com/geocoding/v5/mapbox.places/-73.989,40.733.json?access_token=<span class="token-widget"></span>"</span>

<span class="hljs-comment"># filter results to only include points of interest</span>
curl <span class="hljs-string">"https://api.mapbox.com/geocoding/v5/mapbox.places/-73.989,40.733.json?types=poi&amp;access_token=<span class="token-widget"></span>"</span></pre> 
        </div>
       </div>
       <div data-title="Batch requests" class="keyline-top section contain clearfix " data-reactid="214">
        <div class="space-bottom8 col6 pad2x prose clip" data-reactid="215">
         <h3 id="batch-requests">Batch requests</h3> 
         <p><em>This feature is only available with the <code>mapbox.places-permanent</code> mode.</em></p> 
         <p>Batch requests have the same parameters as normal requests, but can include more than one query by separating queries with the <code>;</code> character. Each query should be URL encoded, but the <code>;</code> character should not be encoded: it should be included verbatim.</p> 
         <p>With the <code>mapbox.places-permanent</code> mode, you can make up to 50 forward or reverse geocoding<a href="https://mapbox.com/help/define-geocoding/" title="Geocoding is the process of taking an address or name of a place and converting it into latitude and longitude values. The Mapbox Geocoding API allows you to performs two types of geocoding: forward geocoding and reverse geocoding." class="auto-glossary-link" rel="noreferrer" target="_blank">?</a> queries in a single request. The response is an array of individual geocoder responses. Each query in a batch request counts individually against your account's rate limits.</p> 
        </div>
        <div class="space-bottom4 col6 pad2 prose clip fill-light space-top5" data-reactid="216">
         <pre class="hljs">curl <span class="hljs-string">"https://api.mapbox.com/geocoding/v5/mapbox.places-permanent/20001;20009;22209.json?access_token=<span class="token-widget"></span>"</span></pre> 
        </div>
       </div>
       <div data-title="Directions" class="keyline-top section contain clearfix " data-reactid="217">
        <div class="space-bottom8 col6 pad2x prose clip" data-reactid="218">
         <h2 id="directions">Directions</h2> 
         <p>The Mapbox Directions API will show you how to get where you're going. With the Directions API, you can:</p> 
         <ul> 
          <li>calculate optimal driving, walking, and cycling routes</li> 
          <li>produce turn-by-turn instructions</li> 
          <li>produce routes with up to 25 coordinates anywhere on earth</li> 
         </ul> 
         <p>This API supports four different routing profiles:</p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><code>mapbox/driving-traffic</code> for automotive routing. This profile factors in current and historic traffic conditions to avoid slowdowns. Traffic is available in <a href="./pages/traffic-countries.html">these supported geographies</a></li> 
          <li><code>mapbox/driving</code> for automotive routing. This profile shows the fastest routes by preferring high-speed roads, like highways.</li> 
          <li><code>mapbox/walking</code> for pedestrian and hiking routing. This profile shows the shortest path by using sidewalks and trails.</li> 
          <li><code>mapbox/cycling</code> for bicycle routing. This profile shows routes that are short and safer for cyclists by avoiding highways and preferring streets with bike lanes.</li> 
         </ul> 
         <p>Swift and Objective-C support for Directions is provided by the <a href="https://github.com/mapbox/MapboxDirections.swift">MapboxDirections.swift</a> library.</p> 
         <p><strong>Restrictions and limits</strong></p> 
         <ul> 
          <li>Directions requests must specify at least two waypoints as starting &amp; ending points. Requests using <code>driving</code>, <code>walking</code>, and <code>cycling</code> profiles can specify up to 25 total waypoints along the route. Requests using the <code>driving-traffic</code> profile can specify up to 3 waypoints.</li> 
          <li>Traffic coverage for the <code>driving-traffic</code> profile is available in <a href="./pages/traffic-countries.html">supported geographies</a>. Requests to this profile revert to <code>driving</code> profile results for areas without traffic coverage.</li> 
          <li>Maximum 60 requests per minute</li> 
          <li>Computing route alternatives is not supported on the <code>driving-traffic</code> profile.</li> 
         </ul> 
        </div>
       </div>
       <div data-title="Retrieve directions" class="keyline-top section contain clearfix " data-reactid="219">
        <div class="space-bottom8 col6 pad2x prose clip" data-reactid="220">
         <h3 id="retrieve-directions">Retrieve directions</h3> 
         <p><a href="https://www.mapbox.com/api-playground/#/directions/">Try this in API Playground</a></p> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>URL Parameter</th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>profile</code></td> 
            <td>Routing profile; either <code>mapbox/driving-traffic</code> , <code>mapbox/driving</code> , <code>mapbox/walking</code> , or <code>mapbox/cycling</code></td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>coordinates</code></td> 
            <td>Semicolon-separated list of <code>{longitude},{latitude}</code> coordinate pairs to visit in order; there can be between 2 and 25 coordinates.</td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table> 
         <p>The response may be altered with optional query parameters:</p> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>Query Parameter</th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>alternatives</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>Whether to try to return alternative routes. An alternative is classified as a route that is significantly different then the fastest route, but also still reasonably fast. Not in all circumtances such a route exists. At the moment at most one alternative can be returned. Can be <code>true</code> or <code>false</code> (default).</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>geometries</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>Format of the returned geometry. Allowed values are: <code>geojson</code> (as <a href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc7946#appendix-A.2">LineString</a> ), <code>polyline</code> ( <a href="https://developers.google.com/maps/documentation/utilities/polylinealgorithm">documentation</a> ) with precision 5, <code>polyline6</code> ( <a href="https://developers.google.com/maps/documentation/utilities/polylinealgorithm">documentation</a> polyline with precision 6). The default value is <code>polyline</code> .</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>overview</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>Type of returned overview geometry. Can be <code>full</code> (the most detailed geometry available), <code>simplified</code> (a simplified version of the full geometry), or <code>false</code> (no overview geometry). The default is <code>simplified</code> .</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>radiuses</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>Maximum distance in meters that each coordinate is allowed to move when snapped to a nearby road segment. There must be as many radiuses as there are coordinates in the request, each separated by <code>;</code> . Values can be any number greater than 0 or they can be the string <code>unlimited</code> . If no routable road is found within the radius, a <code>NoSegment</code> error is returned.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>steps</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>Whether to return steps and turn-by-turn instructions. Can be <code>true</code> or <code>false</code> . The default is <code>false</code> .</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>continue_straight</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>Sets allowed direction of travel when departing intermediate waypoints. If <code>true</code> the route will continue in the same direction of travel. If <code>false</code> the route may continue in the opposite direction of travel. Defaults to <code>true</code> for <code>mapbox/driving</code> and <code>false</code> for <code>mapbox/walking</code> and <code>mapbox/cycling</code> .</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>bearings</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>Used to filter the road segment the waypoint will be placed on by direction and dictates the angle of approach. This option should always be used in conjunction with the <code>radiuses</code> parameter. The parameter takes two values per waypoint: the first is an angle clockwise from true north between 0 and 360. The second is the range of degrees the angle can deviate by. We recommend a value of 45° or 90° for the range, as bearing measurements tend to be inaccurate. This is useful for making sure we reroute vehicles on new routes that continue traveling in their current direction. A request that does this would provide bearing and radius values for the first waypoint and leave the remaining values empty. If provided, the list of bearings must be the same length as the list of waypoints, but you can skip a coordinate and show its position with the <code>;</code> separator.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>annotations</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>Whether or not to return additional metadata along the route. Possible values are: <code>duration</code> , <code>distance</code> , <code>speed</code> and <code>congestion</code> . Several annotations can be used by separating them with <code>,</code> . See the <a href="#routeleg-object">RouteLeg object</a> for more details on what is included with annotations.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>language</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>Language of returned turn-by-turn text instructions. See <a href="#instructions-languages">supported languages</a> . The default is <code>en</code> for English.</td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table> 
         <p>Unrecognized options in the query string result in an <code>InvalidInput</code> error.</p> 
        </div>
        <div class="space-bottom4 col6 pad2 prose clip fill-light space-top5" data-reactid="221">
         <div class="endpoint dark fill-dark round "> 
          <div class="round-left pad0y pad1x fill-lighten0 code small endpoint-method">
           GET
          </div> 
          <div class="pad0 code small endpoint-url">
           https://api.mapbox.com/directions/v5/
           <span class="strong">{profile}</span>/
           <span class="strong">{coordinates}</span>
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <h4 id="example-request-35">Example request</h4> 
         <pre class="hljs"><span class="hljs-comment"># request directions with no additional options</span>
curl <span class="hljs-string">"https://api.mapbox.com/directions/v5/mapbox/cycling/-122.42,37.78;-77.03,38.91?access_token=<span class="token-widget"></span>"</span>

<span class="hljs-comment"># request directions with steps and alternatives</span>
curl <span class="hljs-string">"https://api.mapbox.com/directions/v5/mapbox/cycling/-122.42,37.78;-77.03,38.91?steps=true&amp;alternatives=true&amp;access_token=<span class="token-widget"></span>"</span>

<span class="hljs-comment"># request directions with radiuses and polyline response</span>
curl <span class="hljs-string">"https://api.mapbox.com/directions/v5/mapbox/driving/13.4301,52.5109;13.4265,52.5080;13.4194,52.5072?radiuses=40;;100&amp;geometries=polyline&amp;access_token=<span class="token-widget"></span>"</span>

<span class="hljs-comment"># specify bearings</span>
curl <span class="hljs-string">"https://api.mapbox.com/directions/v5/mapbox/driving/13.4301,52.5109;13.4265,52.5080;13.4316,52.5021?bearings=60,45;;45,45&amp;radiuses=100;100;100&amp;access_token=<span class="token-widget"></span>"</span></pre> 
        </div>
       </div>

       <div data-title="Directions response object" class="keyline-top section contain clearfix " data-reactid="224">
        <div class="space-bottom8 col6 pad2x prose clip" data-reactid="225">
         <h3 id="directions-response-object">Directions response object</h3> 
         <ul> 
          <li><code>code</code>: String indicating the state of the response. This is a separate code than the HTTP status code. On normal valid responses, the value will be <code>Ok</code>.</li> 
          <li><code>waypoints</code>: Array of <a href="#waypoint-object"><code>Waypoint</code></a> objects. Each waypoints is an input coordinate snapped to the road and path network. The waypoints appear in the array in the order of the input coordinates.</li> 
          <li><code>routes</code>: Array of <a href="#route-object"><code>Route</code></a> objects ordered by descending recommendation rank. May contain at most two routes.</li> 
         </ul> 
        </div>

       <div data-title="Waypoint object" class="keyline-top section contain clearfix " data-reactid="227">
        <div class="space-bottom8 col6 pad2x prose clip" data-reactid="228">
         <h3 id="waypoint-object">Waypoint object</h3> 
         <p>An input coordinate snapped to the roads network.</p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><code>name</code>: String with the name of the way the coordinate snapped to</li> 
          <li><code>location</code>: Array of <code>[ longitude, latitude ]</code> for the snapped coordinate</li> 
         </ul> 
        </div>
        <div class="space-bottom4 col6 pad2 prose clip fill-light space-top5" data-reactid="229">
         <h4 id="example-waypoint-object">Example Waypoint object</h4> 
         <pre class="hljs">{
    <span class="hljs-attr">"name"</span>: <span class="hljs-string">"Kirkjubøarvegur"</span>,
    <span class="hljs-attr">"location"</span>: [
        <span class="hljs-number">-6.80897</span>,
        <span class="hljs-number">62.000075</span>
    ]
}</pre> 
        </div>
       </div>
       <div data-title="Route object" class="keyline-top section contain clearfix " data-reactid="230">
        <div class="space-bottom8 col6 pad2x prose clip" data-reactid="231">
         <h3 id="route-object">Route object</h3> 
         <p>A route through (potentially multiple) waypoints.</p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><code>distance</code>: Float indicating the distance traveled in meters</li> 
          <li><code>duration</code>: Float indicating the estimated travel time in seconds</li> 
          <li><code>weight</code>: Float indicating the weight in units described by <code>weight_name</code></li> 
          <li><code>weight_name</code>: String indicating which weight was used. The default is <code>routability</code> which is duration based, with additional penalties for less desirable maneuvers.</li> 
          <li><code>geometry</code>: Depending on the <code>geometries</code> parameter this is a <a href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc7946#appendix-A.2">GeoJSON LineString</a> or a <a href="https://developers.google.com/maps/documentation/utilities/polylinealgorithm">Polyline string</a>. Depending on the <code>overview</code> parameter this is the complete route geometry (<code>full</code>), a simplified geometry to the zoom level at which the route can be displayed in full (<code>simplified</code>), or is not included (<code>false</code>).</li> 
          <li><code>legs</code>: Array of <a href="#routeleg-object"><code>RouteLeg</code></a> objects</li> 
         </ul> 
        </div>
        <div class="space-bottom4 col6 pad2 prose clip fill-light space-top5" data-reactid="232">
         <h4 id="example-route-object">Example Route object</h4> 
         <pre class="hljs">{
    <span class="hljs-attr">"duration"</span>: <span class="hljs-number">88.4</span>,
    <span class="hljs-attr">"distance"</span>: <span class="hljs-number">830.4</span>,
    <span class="hljs-attr">"weight"</span>: <span class="hljs-number">88.4</span>,
    <span class="hljs-attr">"weight_name"</span>: <span class="hljs-string">"routability"</span>,
    <span class="hljs-attr">"geometry"</span>: <span class="hljs-string">"oklyJ`{ph@yBuY_F{^_FxJoBrBs@d@mAT"</span>,
    <span class="hljs-attr">"legs"</span>: [ ]
}</pre> 
        </div>
       </div>
       <div data-title="RouteLeg object" class="keyline-top section contain clearfix " data-reactid="233">
        <div class="space-bottom8 col6 pad2x prose clip" data-reactid="234">
         <h3 id="routeleg-object">RouteLeg object</h3> 
         <p>A route between only two waypoints.</p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><code>distance</code>: Number indicating the distance traveled in meters</li> 
          <li><code>duration</code>: Number indicating the estimated travel time in seconds</li> 
          <li><code>steps</code>: Depending on the <code>steps</code> parameter, either an Array of <a href="#routestep-object"><code>RouteStep</code></a> objects (<code>true</code>, default) or an empty array (<code>false</code>)</li> 
          <li><code>summary</code>: Depending on the <code>summary</code> parameter, either a String summarizing the route (<code>true</code>, default) or an empty String (<code>false</code>)</li> 
          <li><code>annotation</code>: An annotations object that contains additional details about each line segment along the route geometry. Each entry in an annotations field corresponds to a coordinate along the route geometry.</li> 
         </ul> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th><code>annotation</code></th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>distance</code></td> 
            <td>The distance, in meters, between each pair of coordinates</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>duration</code></td> 
            <td>The duration, in seconds, between each pair of coordinates</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>speed</code></td> 
            <td>The speed, in meters per second, between each pair of coordinates</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>congestion</code></td> 
            <td>The congestion level between each pair of coordinates, described as one of <code>severe</code> , <code>heavy</code> , <code>moderate</code> , <code>low</code> or <code>unknown</code></td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table> 
         <p><code>congestion</code> is the speed with traffic compared with speed with no traffic. A break down is below:</p> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>Congestion</th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>low</code></td> 
            <td>between 0% and 20% greater than non-traffic speeds</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>moderate</code></td> 
            <td>between 20% and 60% greater than non-traffic speeds</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>heavy</code></td> 
            <td>between 60% and 80% greater than non-traffic speeds</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>severe</code></td> 
            <td>between 80% and 100% greater than non-traffic speeds</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>unknown</code></td> 
            <td>this information is unavailable</td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table> 
        </div>
        <div class="space-bottom4 col6 pad2 prose clip fill-light space-top5" data-reactid="235">
         <h4 id="example-routeleg-object">Example RouteLeg object</h4> 
         <pre class="hljs">{

    <span class="hljs-attr">"steps"</span>: [],
    <span class="hljs-attr">"summary"</span>: <span class="hljs-string">""</span>
}</pre> 
        </div>
       </div>
       <div data-title="RouteStep object" class="keyline-top section contain clearfix " data-reactid="236">
        <div class="space-bottom8 col6 pad2x prose clip" data-reactid="237">
         <h3 id="routestep-object">RouteStep object</h3> 
         <p>Includes one <code>StepManeuver</code> object and travel to the following <code>RouteStep</code>.</p> 
         <ul> 
          <li> <p><code>distance</code>: Number indicating the distance traveled in meters from the maneuver to the next <code>RouteStep</code>.</p> </li> 
          <li> <p><code>duration</code>: Number indicating the estimated time traveled time in seconds from the maneuver to the next <code>RouteStep</code>.</p> </li> 
          <li> <p><code>geometry</code>: Depending on the <code>geometries</code> parameter this is a <a href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc7946#appendix-A.2">GeoJSON LineString</a> or a <a href="https://developers.google.com/maps/documentation/utilities/polylinealgorithm">Polyline string</a> representing the full route geometry from this <code>RouteStep</code> to the next <code>RouteStep</code></p> </li> 
          <li> <p><code>name</code>: String with the name of the way along which the travel proceeds</p> </li> 
          <li> <p><code>ref</code>: Any <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Road_designation_or_abbreviation">road designations</a> associated with the road or path leading from this step’s maneuver to the next step’s maneuver. Optionally included, if data is available. If <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Concurrency_(road)">multiple road designations</a> are associated with the road, they are separated by semicolons. A road designation typically consists of an alphabetic network code (identifying the road type or numbering system), a space or hyphen, and a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Route_number">route number</a>. You should not assume that the network code is globally unique: for example, a network code of “NH” may appear on a “National Highway” or “New Hampshire”. Moreover, a route number may not even uniquely identify a road within a given network.</p> </li> 
          <li> <p><code>destinations</code>: String with the destinations of the way along which the travel proceeds. Optionally included, if data is available.</p> </li> 
          <li> <p><code>exits</code>: String with the exit numbers or names of the way. Optionally included, if data is available.</p> </li> 
          <li> <p><code>mode</code>: String indicating the mode of transportation. Possible values:</p> 
           <ul> 
            <li>For <code>mapbox/driving</code>: <code>driving</code>, <code>ferry</code>, <code>unaccessible</code></li> 
            <li>For <code>mapbox/walking</code>: <code>walking</code>, <code>ferry</code>, <code>unaccessible</code></li> 
            <li>For <code>mapbox/cycling</code>: <code>cycling</code>, <code>walking</code>, <code>ferry</code>, <code>train</code>, <code>unaccessible</code></li> 
           </ul> </li> 
          <li> <p><code>maneuver</code>: One <a href="#stepmaneuver-object"><code>StepManeuver</code></a> object</p> </li> 
          <li> <p><code>intersections</code>: Array of objects representing all intersections along the step.</p> 
           <ul> 
            <li><code>location</code>: A [longitude, latitude] pair describing the location of the turn.</li> 
            <li><code>bearings</code>: A list of bearing values (for example [0,90,180,270]) that are available at the intersection. The bearings describe all available roads at the intersection.</li> 
            <li> <p><code>classes</code>: An array of strings signifying the classes of the road exiting the intersection. Possible values:</p> 
             <ul> 
              <li><code>toll</code>: the road continues on a toll road</li> 
              <li><code>ferry</code>: the road continues on a ferry</li> 
              <li><code>restricted</code>: the road continues on with access restrictions</li> 
              <li><code>motorway</code>: the road continues on a motorway</li> 
             </ul> </li> 
            <li><code>entry</code>: A list of entry flags, corresponding in a 1:1 relationship to the bearings. A value of true indicates that the respective road could be entered on a valid route. false indicates that the turn onto the respective road would violate a restriction.</li> 
            <li><code>in</code>: Index into bearings/entry array. Used to calculate the bearing before the turn. Namely, the clockwise angle from true north to the direction of travel before the maneuver/passing the intersection. To get the bearing in the direction of driving, the bearing has to be rotated by a value of 180. The value is not supplied for departure maneuvers.</li> 
            <li><code>out</code>: Index into the bearings/entry array. Used to extract the bearing after the turn. Namely, The clockwise angle from true north to the direction of travel after the maneuver/passing the intersection. The value is not supplied for arrive maneuvers.</li> 
            <li><code>lanes</code>: Array of <a href="#lane-object"><code>Lane</code></a> objects that represent the available turn lanes at the intersection. If no lane information is available for an intersection, the <code>lanes</code> property will not be present.</li> 
           </ul> </li> 
         </ul> 
        </div>
        <div class="space-bottom4 col6 pad2 prose clip fill-light space-top5" data-reactid="238">
         <h4 id="example-routestep-object">Example RouteStep object</h4> 
         <pre class="hljs">{
    <span class="hljs-attr">"intersections"</span>: [
      {
        <span class="hljs-attr">"out"</span>: <span class="hljs-number">1</span>,
        <span class="hljs-attr">"location"</span>: [
          <span class="hljs-number">13.424671</span>,
          <span class="hljs-number">52.508812</span>
        ],
        <span class="hljs-attr">"bearings"</span>: [
          <span class="hljs-number">120</span>,
          <span class="hljs-number">210</span>,
          <span class="hljs-number">300</span>
        ],
        <span class="hljs-attr">"entry"</span>: [
          <span class="hljs-literal">false</span>,
          <span class="hljs-literal">true</span>,
          <span class="hljs-literal">true</span>
        ],
        <span class="hljs-attr">"in"</span>: <span class="hljs-number">0</span>
      }
    ],
    <span class="hljs-attr">"geometry"</span>: <span class="hljs-string">"asn_Ie_}pAdKxG"</span>,
    <span class="hljs-attr">"maneuver"</span>: {
      <span class="hljs-attr">"bearing_after"</span>: <span class="hljs-number">202</span>,
      <span class="hljs-attr">"type"</span>: <span class="hljs-string">"turn"</span>,
      <span class="hljs-attr">"modifier"</span>: <span class="hljs-string">"left"</span>,
      <span class="hljs-attr">"bearing_before"</span>: <span class="hljs-number">299</span>,
      <span class="hljs-attr">"location"</span>: [
        <span class="hljs-number">13.424671</span>,
        <span class="hljs-number">52.508812</span>
      ],
      <span class="hljs-attr">"instruction"</span>: <span class="hljs-string">"Turn left onto Adalbertstraße"</span>
    },
    <span class="hljs-attr">"duration"</span>: <span class="hljs-number">59.1</span>,
    <span class="hljs-attr">"distance"</span>: <span class="hljs-number">236.9</span>,
    <span class="hljs-attr">"weight"</span>: <span class="hljs-number">59.1</span>,
    <span class="hljs-attr">"name"</span>: <span class="hljs-string">"Adalbertstraße"</span>,
    <span class="hljs-attr">"mode"</span>: <span class="hljs-string">"driving"</span>
}</pre> 
        </div>
       </div>
       <div data-title="StepManeuver object" class="keyline-top section contain clearfix " data-reactid="239">
        <div class="space-bottom8 col6 pad2x prose clip" data-reactid="240">
         <h3 id="stepmaneuver-object">StepManeuver object</h3> 
         <ul> 
          <li><code>location</code>: Array of <code>[ longitude, latitude ]</code> coordinates for the point of the maneuver</li> 
          <li><code>bearing_before</code>: Number between 0 and 360 indicating the clockwise angle from true north to the direction of travel right before the maneuver</li> 
          <li><code>bearing_after</code>: Number between 0 and 360 indicating the clockwise angle from true north to the direction of travel right after the maneuver</li> 
          <li><code>instruction</code>: A human-readable instruction of how to execute the returned maneuver</li> 
          <li><code>type</code>: String indicating the type of maneuver</li> 
          <li><code>modifier</code> Optional String indicating the direction change of the maneuver</li> 
         </ul> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th><code>modifier</code></th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>uturn</code></td> 
            <td>indicates reversal of direction, <code>type</code> can be <code>turn</code> or <code>continue</code> when staying on the same road</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>sharp right</code></td> 
            <td>a sharp right turn</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>right</code></td> 
            <td>a normal turn to the right</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>slight right</code></td> 
            <td>a slight turn to the right</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>straight</code></td> 
            <td>no relevant change in direction</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>slight left</code></td> 
            <td>a slight turn to the left</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>left</code></td> 
            <td>a normal turn to the left</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>sharp left</code></td> 
            <td>a sharp turn to the left</td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table> 
         <p>The list of turns without a modifier is limited to: <code>depart</code> / <code>arrive</code>. If the source<a href="https://mapbox.com/help/define-source/" title="A source supplies data to be shown on maps that use Mapbox GL. Sources are defined by the Mapbox Style Specification, and are used with style layers to visually represent the source data on to a map. Specific source types may not be supported depending on which platform you're developing on, so refer to platform-specific documentation when adding sources to your map." class="auto-glossary-link" rel="noreferrer" target="_blank">?</a> / target location is close enough to the <code>depart</code> / <code>arrive</code> location, no modifier will be given.</p> 
         <p>The meaning depends on the <code>type</code> property.</p> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th><code>type</code></th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>depart</code> / <code>arrive</code></td> 
            <td><code>modifier</code> indicates the position of departure point and arrival point in relation to the current direction of travel</td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table> 
         <p>New properties (potentially depending on <code>type</code>) may be introduced in the future without an API version change.</p> 
        </div>
        <div class="space-bottom4 col6 pad2 prose clip fill-light space-top5" data-reactid="241">
         <h4 id="example-stepmaneuver-object">Example StepManeuver object</h4> 
         <pre class="hljs">{
    <span class="hljs-attr">"bearing_before"</span>: <span class="hljs-number">299</span>,
    <span class="hljs-attr">"bearing_after"</span>: <span class="hljs-number">202</span>,
    <span class="hljs-attr">"type"</span>: <span class="hljs-string">"turn"</span>,
    <span class="hljs-attr">"modifier"</span>: <span class="hljs-string">"left"</span>,
    <span class="hljs-attr">"location"</span>: [
        <span class="hljs-number">13.424671</span>,
        <span class="hljs-number">52.508812</span>
    ],
    <span class="hljs-attr">"instruction"</span>: <span class="hljs-string">"Turn left onto Adalbertstraße"</span>
}</pre> 
        </div>
       </div>
       <div data-title="Maneuver types" class="keyline-top section contain clearfix " data-reactid="242">
        <div class="space-bottom8 col6 pad2x prose clip" data-reactid="243">
         <h3 id="maneuver-types">Maneuver types</h3> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th><code>type</code></th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>turn</code></td> 
            <td>a basic turn into direction of the modifier</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>new name</code></td> 
            <td>the road name changes (after a mandatory turn)</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>depart</code></td> 
            <td>indicates departure from a leg</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>arrive</code></td> 
            <td>indicates arrival to a destination of a leg</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>merge</code></td> 
            <td>merge onto a street</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>on ramp</code></td> 
            <td>take a ramp to enter a highway</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>off ramp</code></td> 
            <td>take a ramp to exit a highway</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>fork</code></td> 
            <td>take the left/right side of a fork</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>end of road</code></td> 
            <td>road ends in a T intersection</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>continue</code></td> 
            <td>continue on a street after a turn</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>roundabout</code></td> 
            <td>traverse roundabout, has additional property <code>exit</code> in <a href="#routestep-object"><code>RouteStep</code></a> containing the exit number. The modifier specifies the direction of entering the roundabout.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>rotary</code></td> 
            <td>a traffic circle. While very similar to a larger version of a roundabout, it does not necessarily follow roundabout rules for right of way. It can offer <code>rotary_name</code> and / or <code>rotary_pronunciation</code> parameters located in the <a href="#routestep-object"><code>RouteStep</code></a> object in addition to the <code>exit</code> property.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>roundabout turn</code></td> 
            <td>small roundabout that is treated as an intersection</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>notification</code></td> 
            <td>change of driving conditions, e.g. change of <code>mode</code> from <code>driving</code> to <code>ferry</code></td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table> 
        </div>
       </div>
       <div data-title="Lane object" class="keyline-top section contain clearfix " data-reactid="244">
        <div class="space-bottom8 col6 pad2x prose clip" data-reactid="245">
         <h3 id="lane-object">Lane object</h3> 
         <p>Available turn lanes at the intersection. Lanes are provided in their order on the street, from left to right.</p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><code>valid</code>: Boolean value for whether this lane can be taken to complete the maneuver. For instance, if the lane array has four objects and the first two are marked as valid, then the driver can take either of the left lanes and stay on the route.</li> 
          <li><code>indications</code>: Array of signs for each turn lane. There can be multiple signs. For example, a turning lane can have a sign with an arrow pointing left and another sign with an arrow pointing straight.</li> 
         </ul> 
        </div>
        <div class="space-bottom4 col6 pad2 prose clip fill-light space-top5" data-reactid="246">
         <h4 id="example-lane-object">Example Lane object</h4> 
         <pre class="hljs">{
    <span class="hljs-attr">"valid"</span>: <span class="hljs-literal">true</span>,
    <span class="hljs-attr">"indications"</span>: [
        <span class="hljs-string">"left"</span>
    ]
}</pre> 
        </div>
       </div>
       <div data-title="Directions errors" class="keyline-top section contain clearfix " data-reactid="247">
        <div class="space-bottom8 col6 pad2x prose clip" data-reactid="248">
         <h3 id="directions-errors">Directions errors</h3> 
         <p>On error, the server responds with different HTTP status codes. For responses with HTTP status codes lower than <code>500</code>, the JSON response body includes the code property, which may be used by client programs to manage control flow. The response body may also include a message property, with a human-readable explanation of the error. If a server error occurs, the HTTP status code will be 500 or higher and the response will not include a <code>code</code> property.</p> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>Response body <code>code</code></th> 
            <th>HTTP status code</th> 
            <th>comment</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>Ok</code></td> 
            <td><code>200</code></td> 
            <td>Normal success case</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>NoRoute</code></td> 
            <td><code>200</code></td> 
            <td>There was no route found for the given coordinates. Check for impossible routes (e.g. routes over oceans without ferry connections).</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>NoSegment</code></td> 
            <td><code>200</code></td> 
            <td>No road segment could be matched for coordinates. Check for coordinates too far away from a road.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>ProfileNotFound</code></td> 
            <td><code>404</code></td> 
            <td>Use a valid profile as described <a href="#directions">above</a></td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>InvalidInput</code></td> 
            <td><code>422</code></td> 
            <td>The given request was not valid. The <code>message</code> key of the response will hold an explanation of the invalid input.</td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table> 
         <p>This documentation is for the <code>v5</code> API. <a href="./pages/directions-v4.html">See the documentation for the legacy <code>v4</code> API</a>.</p> 
        </div>
       </div>
       <div data-title="Map Matching" class="keyline-top section contain clearfix " data-reactid="249">
        <div class="space-bottom8 col6 pad2x prose clip" data-reactid="250">
         <h2 id="map-matching">Map Matching</h2> 
         <p>The Mapbox Map Matching API snaps fuzzy, inaccurate traces from a GPS unit or a phone to the OpenStreetMap<a href="https://mapbox.com/help/define-osm/" title="OpenStreetMap is a collaborative map of the world that creates a worldwide base map that anyone can contribute to. OpenStreetMap's data is free to share and use. The Mapbox Streets tileset source data is derived from OpenStreetMap. The routing network that powers our Directions API and related APIs is also based on OpenStreetMap." class="auto-glossary-link" rel="noreferrer" target="_blank">?</a> road and path network using the Directions API. This produces clean paths that can be displayed on a map or used for other analysis.</p> 
         <p><strong>Limits</strong></p> 
         <ul> 
          <li>Maximum 60 requests per minute</li> 
          <li>Maximum 100 coordinates per request</li> 
          <li>Results must be displayed on a Mapbox map using one of our <a href="https://mapbox.com/developers">libraries or SDKs</a></li> 
         </ul> 
         <p>For high volume or other use cases, <a href="https://mapbox.com/contact/">contact us</a>.</p> 
        </div>
       </div>
       <div data-title="Retrieve a match" class="keyline-top section contain clearfix " data-reactid="251">
        <div class="space-bottom8 col6 pad2x prose clip" data-reactid="252">
         <h3 id="retrieve-a-match">Retrieve a match</h3> 
         <p>Returns a path on the road and path network closest to the input traces.</p> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>URL Parameter</th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>profile</code></td> 
            <td>A directions profile ID; either <code>mapbox/driving</code> , <code>mapbox/driving-traffic</code> , <code>mapbox/walking</code> , or <code>mapbox/cycling</code></td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>coordinates</code></td> 
            <td>Semicolon-separated list of <code>{longitude},{latitude}</code> coordinate pairs to visit in order; there can be between 2 and 100 coordinates.</td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table> 
         <table> 
          <thead> 
           <tr> 
            <th>Query Parameter</th> 
            <th>Description</th> 
           </tr> 
          </thead> 
          <tbody> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>geometries</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>Format of the returned geometry. Allowed values are: <code>geojson</code> (as <a href="https://tools.ietf.org/html/rfc7946#appendix-A.2">LineString</a> ), <code>polyline</code> ( <a href="https://developers.google.com/maps/documentation/utilities/polylinealgorithm">documentation</a> ) with precision 5, <code>polyline6</code> ( <a href="https://developers.google.com/maps/documentation/utilities/polylinealgorithm">documentation</a> polyline with precision 6). The default value is <code>polyline</code> .</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>radiuses</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>A list of integers in meters indicating the assumed precision of the used tracking device. There must be as many radiuses as there are coordinates in the request, each separated by <code>;</code> . Values can be a number between 0 and 30. Use higher numbers (20-30) for noisy traces and lower numbers (1-10) for clean traces. The default value is 5.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>steps</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>Whether to return steps and turn-by-turn instructions. Can be <code>true</code> or <code>false</code> . The default is <code>false</code> .</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>overview</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>Type of returned overview geometry. Can be <code>full</code> (the most detailed geometry available), <code>simplified</code> (a simplified version of the full geometry), or <code>false</code> (no overview geometry). The default is <code>simplified</code> .</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>timestamps</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>Timestamps corresponding to each coordinate provided in the request; must be numbers in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unix_time">Unix time</a> (seconds since the Unix epoch). There must be as many timestamps as there are coordinates in the request, each separated by <code>;</code> .</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>annotations</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>Whether or not to return additional metadata along the route. Possible values are: <code>duration</code> , <code>distance</code> and <code>speed</code> . Several annotations can be used by separating them with <code>,</code> . See the <a href="#routeleg-object">RouteLeg object</a> for more details on what is included with annotations.</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>tidy</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>Whether or not to transparently remove clusters and re-sample traces for improved map matching results. Can be <code>true</code> or <code>false</code> . The default is <code>false</code> .</td> 
           </tr> 
           <tr> 
            <td><code>language</code> <br> (optional)</td> 
            <td>Language of returned turn-by-turn text instructions. See <a href="#instructions-languages">supported languages</a> . The default is <code>en</code> for English.</td> 
           </tr> 
          </tbody> 
         </table> 
         <p>It is recommended to include timestamps, since they help improve the quality of the matching. The timestamps must be ascending. For best results, your timestamps should have a sample rate of about 5 seconds.</p> 
         <p>Some pre-processing tips to achieve the best results:</p> 
         <ul> 
          <li>The Map Matching API is limited to processing traces with up to 100 coordinates. If you need to process longer traces, you can split the trace and make multiple requests.</li> 
          <li>Clusters of points (like a person waiting at a train crossing for a few minutes) often don't add more information to a trace and can negatively impact map-matching quality. We recommend to tidy the trace: remove clusters and provide a uniform sample rate. You can use the <code>tidy=true</code> query parameter or pre-process your traces with external tools like <a href="https://github.com/mapbox/geojson-tidy">geojson-tidy</a>.</li> 
          <li>Map matching works best with a sample rate of 5 seconds between points. If your trace has a higher sample rate, you may want to downsample your trace.</li> 
         </ul> 
        </div>
        <div class="space-bottom4 col6 pad2 prose clip fill-light space-top5" data-reactid="253">
         <div class="endpoint dark fill-dark round "> 
          <div class="round-left pad0y pad1x fill-lighten0 code small endpoint-method">
           GET
          </div> 
          <div class="pad0 code small endpoint-url">
           /matching/v5/
           <span class="strong">{profile}</span>/
           <span class="strong">{coordinates}</span>.json
          </div> 
         </div> 
         <h4 id="example-request-36">Example request</h4> 
         <pre class="hljs">$ curl <span class="hljs-string">"https://api.mapbox.com/matching/v5/mapbox/driving/-117.1728265285492,32.71204416018209;-117.17288821935652,32.712258556224;-117.17293113470076,32.712443613445814;-117.17292040586472,32.71256999376694;-117.17298477888109,32.712603845608285;-117.17314302921294,32.71259933203019;-117.17334151268004,32.71254065549407?access_token=<span class="token-widget"></span>"</span></pre> 
        </div>
       </div>
       <div data-title="Match response object" class="keyline-top section contain clearfix " data-reactid="254">
        <div class="space-bottom8 col6 pad2x prose clip" data-reactid="255">
         <h3 id="match-response-object">Match response object</h3> 
         <p>With clean matches, only one <a href="#match-object">match object</a> is returned. When the the algorithm cannot decide the correct match between two points, it will omit that line and return several sub-matches as <a href="#match-object">match objects</a>. The higher the number of sub-match <a href="#match-object">match objects</a>, the more likely that the input traces are poorly aligned to the road network.</p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><code>code</code>: a string depicting the state of the response; see below for options</li> 
          <li><code>matchings</code>: an array of <a href="#match-object">Match objects</a></li> 
          <li><code>tracepoints</code>: an array of <a href="#tracepoint-object">Tracepoint objects</a> representing the location an input point was matched with. Array of Waypoint objects representing all input points of the trace in the order they were matched. If a trace point is omitted by map matching because it is an outlier, the entry will be <code>null</code>.</li> 
         </ul> 
        </div>
        <div class="space-bottom4 col6 pad2 prose clip fill-light space-top5" data-reactid="256">
